Okay, now we are on the most important module on this course where you would find your niche.
Why is it so important?
Well, you can start doing videos on YouTube, but if there aren't any views of the same
type of videos you produce, you would not get views either.
That's why I try to maximize my chances to have views.
I'm not talking about posting videos on Facebook to my grandma and her cat and see them.
I'm talking about numbers.
Thanks to YouTube, all the analytics you need are open and you can easily calculate how
much money you would make every month based on competitors in your niche.
Most people who teach YouTube give niches without analysis simply because these niches
have a lot of views.
They show that there is a channel, a million subscribers, a billion of views, but they
do not show the current statistics of the channel.
They don't do a full analysis of this channel and other competitors in the same niche.
And they don't calculate how much these YouTubers earn based on this data every month.
They also don't say that these channels they are shown are the best in the niche while
there are a lot of smaller channels who don't have as much views.

not a long time ago and got small results.

### Video_4.8.1_How_to_find_a_right_freelancer_Arti_Creator.mp4

So these modules for you if you want to create a team to run your YouTube channel or maybe
you want some people to make some of the processes for your like video editing or voiceover.
There's actually two main platforms in the world that have good freelancers.
These are Upwork and Fiverr.
As a freelance video editor, I used to work on Upwork too.
And actually I introduced up 3% of the best freelance video editors on the planet Earth.
These games from the revenue you're getting on the Upwork and I'm on top 3% of the best
freelancers.
You can probably find my profile still.
I also have been published on Upwork social media as a like a success story.
So I was able to do that when I was 20, I think it was like three years ago.
When it comes to hiring freelancers, Upwork is a kind of more premium freelancers while
on Fiverr you would find less, less expensive freelancers.
But sure you can find cheap freelancers on Upwork too, it's just gonna take more time.
And even though I'm gonna recommend you Upwork because here you can find any type of skill
like video editors, like super low end video editors, super high professional video editors
and other freelancers.
I would recommend you first start on both.
But if you have a bigger budget, I would start right away from Upwork, register there and
just post to get freelancers to answer you.
And as a video editor myself, I know what freelancers want from you as a client when
it comes to hiring.
For me and for your future video editors or anyone else that you want to hire is important
to have you long term.
Because if there's a client that says I will give you $500 every month and I would work
with you like a long time, I would go to this client and not to take the client that says
I need a video, you can do it in one week and I would pay like $300 because we would
need to work with that client trying to figure out what he's like, what he doesn't like.
And for that one time job, you're gonna have a lot of revisions.
Well with that long term client, you're gonna make a first couple of videos and then you're
gonna understand why he need it and what you can do and so on.
And for a freelancer, it's important to have you long term.
So when you're gonna do a job pause and write down what you need from the video editor and
what type of channel you have, I would need like 10 videos a month and this is gonna be
long term.
Even if it's not gonna be long term and you would try these or that type of niche and
you're not gonna like it or you're not gonna get views there, you can say to your freelancer
like okay, this is not work and that's it.
And on the other side, if you would write down like I would need a freelancer for five
videos to figure out what's up, sure you're gonna get some answers but they're not gonna
be so interested and the and also that's why I'm saying that is when you're saying like
this is gonna be long term, I'm gonna give you like 510 videos a month or like 30 videos
a month to edit or to do a voiceover or something else, you can ask for a lower price because
when you buying something in batches like 30 videos, I'm not saying like to work right
away pay someone like $500 for a 30 day period for 30 videos, no, it's not working like that.

job is gonna be long term.

## Module 7  Day 20 - Promoting your videos

### Video_7.1_Buy_end_screens_of_your_competitors.mp4

Now, in this tutorial, I'd like to share a technique of buying end screens that I used
for some of my channels, but usually I just boost my new channels with other channels.
So the end screens are the same thing that you add at the end of your video.
I showed how to do that in the previous module, but in this case you're buying a placement
of your latest video on someone else's video, your competitors or creators from similar
niches.
You can buy an end screen on a warmed up channel on the last video you post.
So let's say if you have a video that is coming out tomorrow, you would need to find
a guy who would sell you the end screens.
So when you're gonna post your video, you would already have views from the end screens,
not like three days, four days after.
And usually it takes about a week to warm up the channel.
You can buy end screens when your channel has posted at least five videos.
And that is what I would consider a warm up channel that have five videos at least posted.
Now the best practice here is if the views from the end screens come you within the
first hours after you posted your video and not for a long time, like not in two days
or three days, it should be like in a few hours after you posted the video.
And how do you actually do that?
Well I put the end screens method into three stages.
You have test number one, test number two and final test number three.
Now for the first test you would need to buy at least from 1500 views to 2500 views from
the end screens of your competitors.
Now the second final test would be two days after you bought the views for the first test
and you have no views from the recommendation.
For the second test you can increase the views here, buying from 2500 views to 3500 views.
So basically 1000 views more than you bought at the first test.
And the third test must be done after two, four days, again after your second test.
So if there's no views coming from recommendations after two, four days you can make the third
test and buy up to 4000 views.
And usually after the third test the channel goes to the recommendations and takes off.
But if it doesn't help it's worth letting the channel stand for a week, basically not
posting anything while checking the analytics every day to see if there are any views coming
from recommendations.
If in that week you see that views are starting to come from recommendations you need to immediately
start posting new content and continue as usual.
If you miss that your views growing and post a new video like four days after you started
getting views from recommendations that may not end well for your channel.
And usually you would get the views from recommendations because that's really working with the kids
niches almost all of the time.

Okay, the next method is average view duration trick.
For YouTube, it is really important that you have a good average view duration, which is
how long people watch your videos on average.
So if your channel is struggling to get views, you can make a shorter videos and after you
upload like seven shorter videos, you can upload the same length videos as you had before
you started uploading these short content.
For example, if you have a channel with an eight minute videos, you can create seven
videos that one minute long and publish them as you normally would.
After that, you can start posting eight minute videos or 20 minute videos maybe and that
way YouTube will see that your channel is dropped down even more when you started uploading
these short videos.
